0061251305|5.0|What separates average companies from those that excel?<br /><br />In their ten-year field study of twenty-four thousand people in two dozen organizations, \\"Tribal Leadership\\" authors Dave Logan, John King, and Halee Fischer-Wright found their answer in the relationship between tribes formed by employees (natural formations) and the tribe's leader.<br /><br />Tribes are the basic building block of any large human effort determining how much work gets done and the quality of the work they do. Tribes and tribal leaders create each other. Tribes range in size from 20 to 150 people with small companies generally being one tribe and large companies being a tribe of tribes.<br /><br />\\"Tribal culture exists in stages, going from undermining to egocentric to history making.\\"<br />These five stages (stage 5 outperforms stage 4, etc.) are identified and characterized by the authors - each has its unique way of speaking, type of behavior, and structure of relationships:<br /><br />* Stage one - 2% of all tribes - bind together to get a ahead in a violent and unfair world. Marked by hostility.<br />* Stage two - 25% - passively antagonistic; \\"my life sucks,\\" a cluster of apathetic victims.<br />* Stage three - 49% - \\"I'm great and you are not.\\" Knowledge is power and it is hoarded for control. Trust is hard earned.<br />* Stage four - 22% - \\"We're great.\\" This tribe always has an adversary. Trust is assumed.<br />* Stage five - 2% - language revolves around infinite potential and how the group is going to make history, not to beat a competitor, but to have global impact.  This stage is pure leadership, vision, and inspiration.<br /><br />With this perspective, the authors then get to the heart and soul of the book, outlining the steps, identifying the leverage points, and providing the tools a leader can use to upgrade his/her tribe from one stage to another - with the goal of building a high performance tribe that excels. They have also created a website, [...], as a resource for those wanting more.<br /><br />The tribal cultures of IDEO, CB Richard Ellis' Private Client Group, and She Beads are used throughout the book as examples o emphasize key points.<br /><br />\\"Tribal Leadership\\" provides great value and is a must read for those interested in becoming a better leader and/or those wanting to insure their business strategies succeed rather than fail (70% fail). I have chosen to integrate this book into the limited C-level mentoring I do.<br /><br />See also my review of Seth Godin's \\"Tribes: We Need You to Lead Us.\\"O, CB Richard Ellis' Private Client Group, and She Beads are used throughout the book as examples o emphasize key points.     \\"Tribal Leadership\\" provides great value and is a must read for those interested in becoming a better leader and/or those wanting to insure their business strategies succeed rather than fail (70% fail). B000THIHA4|5.0|I cannot emphasize enough how spectacular this 5-star album is. How much creativity and effort is poured into every single one of these tracks. To me, this is the album that defines Daft Punk - Melodious vocals, well placed beats, perfect timing, and unique musical ideas. One More Time, Aerodynamic, Digital Love, Harder Better Faster Stronger, Something About Us, Voyager, Short Circuit, Face to Face, and Too Long are all quite exceptional tracks, and none of the other songs are mediocre enough to be labeled album filler. Let's get right to the song by song analysis:<br /><br />1. One More Time - 5/5 Stars. This track is absolutely classic. A shimmering music track with perfectly timed vocals and beats. Very fun to dance to. It doesn't matter if you're a techno fan or not. No one can dislike this song.<br /><br />2. Aerodynamic - 5/5 Stars. A remarkable track. Very well put together, with an interesting sound and very rapid notes. This song is very creative, and takes on an almost magical sound from 2:30 to the end. This song is extremely cool. Not one of Daft Punks most famous tracks but it should be.<br /><br />3. Digital Love - 5/5 Stars. Catchy, well timed beat. Cute vocals. Cute lyrics. This is a very feel-good song. Like Aerodynamic, the track gets more and more awesome as the song progresses. At 3:25 a crazy guitar riff is added, giving the song a wild climax to 4:25. Then the song cools down to a peaceful ending.<br /><br />4. Harder Better Faster Stronger- 5/5 Stars. Probably one of Daft Punks most famous songs, and for good reason. This song is perfectly timed with progressive vocals and an irresistible beat. Extremely fun to dance to. It's also fun to see how long you can keep up with the vocals before you run out of breath. It's hard to describe what makes this track so epic. You just have to hear it.<br /><br />5. Crescendolls - 4/5 Stars for techno fans, 3/5 Stars for casual audiences. There's only one word to describe this track: weird. But if you're like me and love music that is creative to the point of strangeness, you will enjoy this track. More casual listeners, however, will think this sounds pretty nasty. This one's harder to dance to. This song is good, but not on the same tier as the first four tracks, and probably too weird for many people.<br /><br />6. Nightvision - 4/5 Stars. There's nothing wrong with this song, except it doesn't feel complete. Well under two minutes long, it doesn't feel like a song. It is also quite un-danceable. To its credit, it is well put together and very soothing to listen to. Again, no real complaint here, just not as epic as the first four tracks.<br /><br />7. Superheroes - 4/5 Stars. A good track. Steady beat. Well timed. Danceable. However, the lyrics are extremely repetitive, which isn't a problem for me, but take it down a notch from the awesome vocals in One More Time, Digital Love, and Harder Better Faster Stronger. Altogether, a solid track, but not outstanding.<br /><br />8. High Life - 4/5 Stars for techno fans, 3/5 Stars for casual listeners. Same story as Crescendolls. A high pitched voice shouting BAAAM, BUUUM, BAAAM, BUUM over and over. This song is just silly. But, as a fan of creatively weird techno I still enjoy listening to it.<br /><br />9. Something About Us - 5/5 Stars. A sublime, relaxing song with touching vocals. Like Nightvision, not a danceable song. I love this track. Like Digital Love, it shows that techno can make love songs too, and good ones at that.<br /><br />10. Voyager - 5/5 Stars. This song is delightful. A distorted bassline under a shimmering track. At 2:16 a quick xylophone-ish note progression is added, meshing perfectly with the first two musical elements. Not very danceable, but overall as good as the first four tracks.<br /><br />11.Veridis Quo - 4/5 Stars. Similar to Nightvision, only a complete song. It progresses very slowly, but very naturally, and grows more and more complex. Soothing to listen to, but not danceable. A greattrack.<br /><br />12. Short Circuit- 5/5 Stars for techno fans, 3/5 stars for casual listeners. Excellent song from 0:00-1:40. The first 1:40 is great for breakdancing and extremely catchy. Then the song slows down, to a riff that grows more and more distorted until the song ends. Near the end the track gets very choppy. Casual listeners will hate this part. As a techno fan I find this intriguing and melodious in its own way. Very creative, very catchy at the beginning and very interesting at the end.<br /><br />13. Face to Face - 5/5 Stars. Brilliant. Creative. Great vocals. Fascinating beat. I would go as far as to call this the best song in the album. The music is all over the place, but somehow makes something perfectly harmonious. We then move on to great vocals with a steady beat in the background. The song also has an interesting message to it, but I'll leave the lyrical interpretation to you. I wish this song was a lot longer. It feels like the ending is way too early, especially for a techno song. I think Daft Punk should've extended this song another 2 minutes. But as it stands, it's still an absolutely brilliant, catchy, danceable song.<br /><br />14.Too Long - 5/5 Stars. Well, it's a 10:00 minute song called \\"Too Long.\\" The question stands- is this song literally too long, or is it 10 minutes of quality music? I would say the latter. It has a natural progression with great vocals and an interesting message. When the beat finally kicks in at 1:38 its very catchy and danceable. The music gradually swells, ebbs, and changes, over the duration of the song, but remains interesting and catchy. An excellent end to the album that is certainly not too long.<br /><br />Discovery is a shining gem among techno albums. Even if you're not much of a techno head, you'll find a great deal of these songs enjoyable. This is the best $9.49 I've spent in my life, but you're making a huge mistake if you leave this page without downloading \\"Face to Face\\" at the very least. Thanks for reading!

Blending riffs from old and new Sabbath styles, \\"Trashed\\" is a great throwback to something like \\"Tomorrow's Dream\\". And the main rhythm is simply \\"Sabbath, Bloody Sabbath\\" sped up!<br /><br />Next, the instrumental \\"Stonehenge\\" lulls the listener into a false sense of serenity before the next track blasts them out of their chair. \\"Disturbing The Priest\\" is possibly the heaviest, most sinister song from Sabbath since their first two or three albums! A riff heavily `borrowed' from Ian Gillan's own \\"Scarabus\\", mixed with lyrics like \\"the Devil and the priest can't exist with one goes away', this makes for one awesome gargantuan heavy metal song!<br /><br />But, my favorite song on the album would have to be the next track \\"Zero The Hero\\" (following a very brief instrumental interlude called \\"The Dark\\"). This is without a doubt the heaviest song ever from Black Sabbath! This is \\"Iron Man\\" meets \\"Into The Void\\" on steroids!<br /><br />The great riffmeister Iommi laid down some blistering tracks here. This is FULL of mean riffs and rhythms that are a glorious throwback to the early days of Sabbath (think \\"Master of Reality\\" and \\"Sabotage\\"). Songs like \\"Trashed\\", \\"Disturbing The Priest\\", \\"Zero The Hero\\", and the title track are true classics!<br /><br />I also believe Geezer played a part in the sound of this album. Listen to \\"Zero the Hero\\", he's all over the place! Matter of fact, Judas Priest blatantly stole Geezer's bass riff from that song for the intro to their song \\"Love Bites\\", which came out later in the same year. And Guns & Roses blatantly stole the entire riff for their \\"Paradise City\\".<br /><br />The sound was SO unique, harkening back to a sound like the very 1st three albums.<br /><br />I have always thought \\"Born Again\\" was one of Sabbath's best albums, of any era. Why? Because when you strip away all the critiques of cover art/lineup/sound mix, \\"Born Again\\" was really getting to the heart of the sound and mood Sabbath achieved with their first album: Ambient, dark, bluesy, ferocious and entirely unique. Much like their debut album, you won't hear another album quite like this. Ever again.<br /><br />The sound mix is \\"bad\\" by a normal standard, but I almost feel it does these songs a service. They are raw, unpolished and powerful. Iommi's riffs are as good as any of the classic Ozzy era stuff. And Gillan....goodness I don't know that you could find a better singer to match the sound and mood of this particular album. His performance here was balls-out (literally, if you know that story) heart on sleeve primal. It's a shame that Gillan himself, along with a large portion of the listening audience, didn't \\"get\\" this album.<br /><br />I firmly believe \\"Born Again\\" was entirely an attempt by Iommi to reinvent the band by taking it back to what made Sabbath great to begin with. Away from the late-Ozzy experimentations of \\"Never Say Die\\" and \\"Technical Ecstasy\\". Away from the ultra-polished D&D gems of the Dio era. This was Sabbath `born again`, as Iommi wished to shape it. Of course that long-term vision failed, but what a great single album document we have with this record.<br /><br />One of the best Black Sabbath albums ever created. \\"Born Again\\" with the iconic Ian Gillan at the helm this time around definitely renewed my appreciation for Black Sabbath. Sabbath's most underrated album. The title track is especially good., possibly one of the most haunting songs in rock history, in my opinion. Ian Gillan's talent for not only singing, but also as a lyricist shown really bright on that one in particular.<br /><br />First of all, let's get something straight, no matter how rough Sabbath's career may have turned in the 80's, their albums never went to any cutout bins! As a matter of fact, this one even placed well on the charts for a brief period.<br /><br />And this version of the band live was probably the most sinister sets that Sabbath ever turned in. Gillan's continuous screaming/singing/screaming amidst the gloom and doom of the titanic Iommi/Butler riffs, this made for one hell of a terrific year for Black Sabbath! They didn't call the album \\"Born Again\\" for nothing!<br /><br />I have a problem (since I am a drummer) with the sound of the drums in the mix on this one, however. Even live, it was the strangest drum sound they ever had. I've recently started to referring to it as the \\"drummer un-friendly album/tour\\". Speaking of drummers, Bill Ward wasn't able to tour for this album, so Sabbath brought in ELO skin basher Bev Bevan.<br /><br />I've been listening to \\"Live at Reading 83\\" (which is one of MANY cd's I have from that tour) and I have to say that the more I listen to it, it is possibly the most 'sinister' that Sabbath had sounded since their first 3 cds. Their set list changed somewhat throughout the tour, but I prefer the \\"Reading Festival\\" list.<br /><br />Ian Gillan made the song \\"Black Sabbath\\" HIS, making Ozzy and RJ Dio sound like amatuers compared to him singing it. The second best is Glenn Hughes, believe it or not, on the \\"Seventh Star\\" tour (well, the 3 or 5 days before he was fired), he REALLY sounds sinister as h*ll! But, my pick will always be Ian Gillan on that one, as well as all the Ozzy songs, for Ian not only screamed his head off, sounding very sinister, he gave the Ozzy-era songs a whole new 'passion' that was missing from any of the other singers versions.<br /><br />As for the cover, why don't BS fans pick on the awful \\"Vol 4\\" cover...Now, that's the WORST Black Sabbath album cover ever in my opinion. The album cover is pure genius, because after all Black Sabbath was truly `Born Again'. People ought to be picking on the god-awful Ozzy \\"Bark At the Moon\\" cover by the same artist, Steve Joule. Now, there was a BAD cover!<br /><br />(Footnote to other reviewers on here: If you don't like the cover, then don't buy the cd! The baby devil is the PERFECT cover for the title they chose.) This is a must for any Black Sabbath fan! Rock on! :>)<br /><br />By the way, this is not a review of the recently released Deluxe Edition. I do find it very ironic however that I mentioned the Reading Festival cd in my review, and then I see that the Reading Festival is added as a bonus cd on the Deluxe Edition. And, as for the bonus song \\"The Fallen\\", while I feel it is a very good song, I see why it was not on the original album, because it sounds more like something from Gillan's solo career, or something from his stint in Deep Purple than it does Sabbath. And, as for the quality of the Deluxe Edition, well, sorry, I have no idea what that is like, and frankly, since I already have all of the \\"bonus\\" stuff on bootleg cd's, well, I really don't see the need to purchase it. B0002XMF5S|5.0|After the \\"Born Again\\" tour ended, Ian Gillan and Bev Bevan took off, leaving Tony Iommi and Geezer Butler yet again in a bad spot, needing to rebuild their band, Black Sabbath. An attempt was made in 84 with the return of Bill Ward, and new-comer vocalist David Donato, but that lasted only for a few photo shoots, and maybe a couple of rehearsals before falling apart. Then in 85 the original Black Sabbath reunited for \\"Live Aid\\", and there were rumors of them reuniting for good. Thank God that didn't happen!<br /><br />Iommi and Butler branched off (or one could say that Butler left Sabbath, and that's the way I see it) to do solo projects. However, Sabbath still owed WB Records a 'Black Sabbath' record, plus WB execs, after hearing what Iommi had recorded with bassist Dave \\"The Beast\\" Spitz, drummer Eric Singer, and vocalist Glenn Hughes (one-time bassist/vocalist for Deep Purple), they urged Iommi to release it under the Black Sabbath name. Something that he would have been a fool not to have done! I've just always hated the 'featuring Tony Iommi' part under the Sabbath name. It was (and still is) a 'catch-22' situation: If it would have been released as a Tony Iommi solo album, critics and fans alike would have bashed it, calling it a Sabbath knock-off, and released as a Sabbath album, it was bashed for not being released as a solo album.<br /><br />However, the album did pretty well, and Sabbath were born again yet again! Opening with the fierce and heavy and fast \\"In For the Kill\\", they let you know from the get go they are back with a vengeance. From the start I was hooked immediately. It took me a while to get used to the whole new 'double bass drum' sound of \\"Turn to Stone\\", love the title track, have been back and forth on \\"Danger Zone\\", and the rest I love as well. The ballad \\"No Stranger To Love\\" reminds me a LOT of earlier Sabbath 'ballads' like \\"You Won't Change Me\\", \\"Changes\\", \\"Solitude\\", et al, even though it is a bit more radio-friendly.<br /><br />Drummer Eric Singer should not only be credited for being one of the greatest drummers in rock (then unknown, stolen from the Lita Ford band, but to go on to working with the likes of Alice Cooper and KISS), but for introducing Sabbath fans to the double bass drum kit sound in the confines of Sabbath. Yes, Bill Ward had a double bass kit, but he was (and still is) a King of the Single Bass, as is Vinnie Appice. The already mentioned \\"In For The Kill\\" and \\"Turn To Stone\\" are solid rockers that are furthered along with Eric's mean kick a** drumming.<br /><br />But, the real treat on this album (if those weren't good enough) are the very bluesy numbers \\"Heart Like A Wheel\\", \\"Angry Heart\\", \\"Danger Zone\\", and \\"In Memory\\" (and the already mentioned \\"No Stranger To Love\\"). This is the blues like only Iommi and Sabbath could play it (and remember, Black Sabbath were a blues group from the outset). Very haunting riffs blended with Hughes' unique soulful blues voice just brings this album to life!<br /><br />And, if that's all not good enough, there is a real great 'mystic' track on here! An instrumental called \\"Sphinx (The Guardian)\\" blends into the title track for one of the best Black Sabbath songs since \\"Heaven And Hell\\" and/or \\"Lonely Is the Word\\" from the \\"Heaven And Hell\\" album.<br /><br />Personally, I am SO glad that this was released as a Black Sabbath cd instead of an Iommi solo project, for if it had been released back then as an Iommi solo project, not only would it have been slammed for already said reasons, but it would have ended up in the same cut-out bins with Jimmy Page's \\"Outrider\\". Does anyone remember that one??? It was actually pretty good. Page should have taken a cue from Iommi and tried calling that a Zep record, and maybe it would still be talked about to this day like \\"Seventh Star\\" is...Then again, maybe not, because this has withstood the test of time because it is great music from a great band.<br /><br />And, this set live was phenomenal! Even though Glenn was fired after only 5 days on the road and the AWESOME Ray Gillen was brought in to replace him, it was a great year for Sabbath live! This version of the band was AWESOME live! They definitely deserved to be called Black Sabbath! So, if for only that, I am so glad this was released as a Sabbath album, for it helped keep them going on through the 90's. This was their price for the battle they were going to wage. The Samurai come off as a selfless lot who sacrifice themselves for the cause of the farmers. Simmons<br /><br />20th Century Fox   2007   96 min   Rated PG-13   Released Apr 15, 2008<br /><br />Video:<br />Video codec: MPEG-4 AVC<br />Video resolution: 1080p<br />Aspect ratio: 1.85:1<br /><br />Audio:<br />English: DTS-HD Master Audio 5.1<br />English: Dolby Digital 5.1<br />French: Dolby Digital 5.1<br />Spanish: Dolby Digital 5.1<br /><br />Subtitles:<br />English SDH, Spanish<br /><br />Disc:<br />50GB Blu-ray Disc<br />Digital copy<br /><br />The Film 5/5<br /><br />Juno was nominated for four Oscars, winning for best original screenplay (Diablo Cody). It was a competitive year with No Country for Old Men and There Will Be Blood dividing six of the major categories between them, but Ellen Page was unlucky not to win in her category. Shot on a budget of $7.5 million, it made $143 million in the USA alone and a further $88 million worldwide.<br /><br />Director Jason Reitman was also responsible for Up in the Air in 2009, which, along with Juno, dealt with subjects in which I had very little interest. But Reitman's mix of drama and comedy works well in both movies and the witty dialogue drives both.<br /><br />Juno is funny throughout, but it's never dumb comedy and it never resorts to gross humor. The story works because we care about the characters and their one-liners fit both their personality and the situation. In short, it feels real. Many comedies assault the viewer with a stream of contrived jokes and it falls flat (for me at least).<br /><br />Juno MacGuff (Page) is 16 and newly-pregnant. We are shown a flashback showing how it happened and who the father is. It turns out to be one of her best friends, Paulie Bleeker (Cera). After telling him, she decides that an abortion is the best course of action, but she changes her mind following a visit to the clinic. She's a smart girl and feels capable of making her own decisions, eventually deciding that adoption may be the best thing for her and the baby.<br /><br />She finds potential parents in an ad and then has the task of telling her father (Simmons) and stepmother (Allison Janney) that she's pregnant. This is where the movie first defies our expectations. Instead of anger and shock, her parents are calm and accepting. They even joke about the situation when she reveals the father. It's so refreshing to see supportive parents rather than the usual stereotypes.<br /><br />Her father wants to go with her to meet the prospective foster parents, Vanessa (Jennifer Garner) and Mark (Bateman). Vanessa desperately wants a baby and is skeptical that Juno will honor the agreement, while Mark is more relaxed about everything. He bonds with Juno when she sees his guitar and they end up singing together.<br /><br />Juno keeps in touch with the couple and forms a friendship with Mark because of their common love of music and movies. I particularly like this sequence because I'm passionate about both subjects and know the power of sharing and talking about such things. It's the main reason that I write about movies. Mark introduces her to Sonic Youth (my favorite band) and Juno shares some of her classic rock and punk albums. It seems that the two might enter into a more serious relationship.<br /><br />Her stepmother teaches her about food supplements and defends Juno when she goes to the hospital and is insulted by the ultrasound technician. It's further evidence that she'll be supported in her choices all the way.<br /><br />Bleeker's face lights up every time he sees Juno. Cera plays the part well and doesn't go over the top. It's a quiet and understated performance, but he makes it clear that she's special to him. She suggests that he date a different girl, but is angry when he does. The two have a showdown and it again becomes clear that they really feel something for each other.<br /><br />There's a touching scene in the shopping mall where Juno encounters Vanessa and sees her playing with a little girl. We see Juno forming the opinion that Vanessa will make a good mother. The scene develops with a meeting between the two in which Vanessa talks to Juno's belly.<br /><br />Her arrangement with Vanessa and Mark is threatened by one occurrence and we wonder how everything will turn out. I won't reveal that here, but it's a good resolution.<br /><br />Another great scene involves a chat between father and daughter. It's a potentially life-changing talk played perfectly by Page and Simmons. It sets into motion events that shape Juno's immediate future. Simmons is so talented. If I were a writer/director, one of the first things I would do is create a starring role for Simmons. He's made his mark with supporting roles, but has so much more to offer.<br /><br />As for Page, what a remarkable talent. She carried such films as Whip It and Hard Candy, and had a major supporting role in Inception. At 24, she has most of her career ahead of her and I'm excited to see how she develops. She's already capable of showing so much emotion and her comic timing is perfect. It will be fun to see what happens over the next decade.<br /><br />One important component of the movie is the soundtrack. Kimya Dawson contributes nine of the songs in the film and they fit the mood and Juno's character perfectly. There's a well-placed Kinks song and bands such as Cat Power and Belle & Sebastian also fit the mood. The highlight is Sonic Youth covering the Carpenters' Superstar, and it's an important part of the plot.<br /><br />Juno isn't a film that will appeal to everyone. Some argue that the dialogue isn't realistic, but I found it so. Who is it aimed at? Teens? Women? Pregnant girls? Many will write it off as falling into one of those categories. That would be a shame because it has a lot more to offer. I'm a 48-year-old man and I found it utterly charming, refreshing, intelligent and genuinely funny.<br /><br />There's a chance it may upset some people because it turns a serious situation into an amusing comedy. Is it saying that it's acceptable to be pregnant at 16? How would you feel as a parent who faced a similar situation? How would you feel if you were a pregnant teen and didn't receive that kind of support and understanding from your parents? I would hope that it can be taken for what it is; a fictional situation. It's more about how the characters react to the situation than anything else.<br /><br />Video Quality 4/5<br />For such a low-budget movie, the look is surprisingly good. The transfer is clean and free from damage, colors are well-represented and detail is good in the vast majority of scenes. I can't quite justify a 4.5, but it's certainly worth a 4. Don't expect a visual feast and you should be pretty happy with the overall look.<br /><br />Audio Quality 4/5<br />Juno is a dialogue-heavy movie that's quiet for the majority of its running time, but the sound still plays an important part. The songs are presented well and when sound is called for, such as in amplified effects in the clinic waiting room, it comes across convincingly.<br /><br />Special Features 5/5<br /><br />It's rare that I watch a movie and immediately tackle all of the special features, and even rarer to watch them again on subsequent viewings. Juno is an exception. I like this world and the quality of the extras makes it worth seeing them more than once, even though they are all in standard definition.<br /><br />Commentary with Jason Reitman and Diablo Cody<br /><br />Deleted Scenes (20:23) - It would be great to see an extended version of the film at some point and most or all of these scenes would fit well. My favorites include Juno singing a song about Paulie in a bar and her real thoughts about Sonic Youth.<br /><br />Gag Reel (5:11)<br /><br />Gag Take (1:57)<br /><br />Crew Music Video (3:12) - A song featuring members of the cast.<br /><br />Screen Tests (22:35) - See how Page, Cera, Thirlby and Simmons earned their roles.<br /><br />Way Beyond \\"Our\\" Maturity Level: Juno-Leah-Bleeker (8:59)<br /><br />Diablo Cody is Totally Boss (8:35) - Showing how Cody went from blogger to writing the screenplay.<br /><br />Jason Reitman for Shizz (8:08) - Showing how Reitman came to direct the movie.<br /><br />Honest to Blog!: Creating Juno (13:01) - Reitman, Cody and some of the cast talking about how the movie came to be made.<br /><br />Fox Movie Channel presents world premiere...Juno (5:26)<br /><br />Fox Movie Channel presents Casting Session: Juno (7:51)<br /><br />Watching Juno is like spending time with an old friend. B000K2NDPM|4.0|As a university teacher I am forever telling my students to \\"Define your terms.\\" Before any Literary  work can be fully judged and evaluated a clear and binding set of parameters must be established; benchmarks against which the piece in question can be compared, contrasted and most importantly evaluated. If no terms are defined, and no frame of reference draw or defined, then there is no way we can evaluate writing, because what are we comparing it to?<br /><br />My problem therefore with this book, is how to evaluate it. What is it? What does it want to be judged as? Where should we put it in the library? Amongst whose company should it sit? These are very fundamental questions that require unambiguous answers if we are to set about processing this work as it clearly deserves to be processed. Whilst I understand this work to be Herr's catharsis, on a more practical level is it a novel? a memoir? a historical document? Is it fiction? non-fiction? Is it journalism? war correspondence? Maybe I could set it in one of these boxes, but it would not sit comfortably in a single one. And the one I might elect might not be the same one Herr would wish it to be read as. It's rather akin to a person of mixed ethnicity going through immigration and not knowing which is the better of the boxes to tick - there being  no one that correctly denotes their ethnicity. All of this confusion does not really allow the Work to be fully appreciated and accurately processed and as I tell my students who don't define their terms correctly, whilst I CAN read your submission -  because I can't accurately appraise it,  your score will suffer as a consequence.<br /><br />To the work:<br /><br />There is no doubt that this is an important piece of social and cultural heritage which undoubtedly adds to the Historical Record for the latter half of the 1960s. However, because it is so clearly a period-piece it suffers somewhat from both its tone and use of language and this is something that makes it difficult reading. Linguistically, the '60s was a fascinating period which gave brief rise to a wealth of youth-driven modes of communication and an abundance of periodic vocabulary. Fortunately (or unfortunately) when the door was closed on flower-power etc. linguistics returned to normal. This work therefore, and the language contained within the prose often reads akin to Shakespeare and therefore requires additional commentary to clarify and contextualize the somewhat dated language.<br /><br />As per the previous point and comments made by other reviewers, this work is a hard slog. Due in part to the aforementioned dated linguistics, and due in part to the 'Gonzo' style of rendering, Herr really does make you take a machete and hack your way through the terrain. Certainly before it lets up in the Fifth Act 'Colleagues' the reader is right there with the action, not necessarily the physical 'blood-and-guts', but rather the spiritual, the metaphysical, the psychological and the ontological.<br /><br />In summation:<br /><br />This is a very fascinating period-piece and a bona-fide part of the Historical Record. It should be read as part of a wider trawl through the unprecedented volume Literature that both the '60s and the Viet Nam War gave rise to. Viewed as a historical document set in the linguistic form of the late '60s 'Counter-Culture', this text works admirable and justifies its longevity and abundant praise. Recommended.Linguistically, the '60s was a fascinating period which gave brief rise to a wealth of youth-driven modes of communication and an abundance of periodic vocabulary. Fortunately (or unfortunately) when the door was closed on flower-power etc. linguistics returned to normal. This work therefore, and the language contained within the prose often reads akin to Shakespeare and therefore requires additional commentary to clarify and contextualize the somewhat dated language. In summation:    This is a very fascinating period-piece and a bona-fide part of the Historical Record. Viewed as a historical document set in the linguistic form of the late '60s 'Counter-Culture', this text works admirable and justifies its longevity and abundant praise. Recommended.

B004LWZW4C|4.0|First, I will say that I am not one to get overly upset with the alterations to character history. So long as the essence of the character remains true I think fans need to be (somewhat) open minded. That is to say, I don't want to see Batman pointlessly using guns or Spider-man being carefree without the underlying burden of his great responsibility, etc. Changing timelines or events can be seen as eXcusable if it allows a more cohesive story. So leaving all eXpectations other than core character traits at the door what can one eXpect from the latest X-men film?     It's become quite difficult to give honest reviews of these (comic book) films. The problem is that so many have been bombarded at us in the last decade, many from the same franchise's, that it has become difficult for any individual film to be judged on its own. Comparisons become unavoidable.     X-men (2000) was a new experience when it first arrived, it had its flaws, but before then nobody had seen a large budget attempt at an ensemble cast superhero movie. It stood out in that regard as a first attempt. Now there is no first attempt eXcuse, people start to judge these films more harshly because they eXpect the filmmakers to learn from previous attempts. That said, X-men: First Class IS a good film.     Further, if you ignore highly regarded comic book movies such as X2, Spider-man 2 and The Dark Knight, this film is eXcellent as a comic book movie. Especially if viewed as a first entry in a new series. It can only be said to suffer the same issues that all first entries in these franchises do - it has too much to do for any of it to feel completely natural and we aren't entirely used to the version of the world being presented yet.     In an attempt to counteract these usual issues the CIA is used as an easy way to explain certain otherwise difficult to explain plot points. They want to keep the story moving and have limited runtime, understood, but it took getting used to for me to accept that Charles and Eric were basically given Cerebro and the Blackbird already built (even if here it is Beast who designed them).     Also, Mystique meeting Charles plays somewhat expository, along the same line there are several other moments that can be said to be shoved in simply because they need to happen, but they are telling so much story with so many new characters that these issues are largely forgiven.     The largest fault anyone could find in this film is that Charles and Eric were played so well anyone would wish for more scenes with them and exploring their friendship, especially given that this was the one film they had a chance to do so before certain events unfolded.     In the POSITIVES (which do outway any negatives), Eric and Charles are played so incredibly well. Fassbender in particular helps one see how this film could easily have been Origins: Magneto while McAvoy brings a welcomed boyish charm to Xavier (though I would have loved to see more of the character's motivations explained or explored by the script). All the actors playing the first class are perfectly cast in their roles. The powers are showcased nicely and action is found throughout in original set pieces that feel fresh. CGI is well done and at least isn't as heavily relied on as say Origins Wolverine. They tell an epic story and the sixties setting helps the film amazingly, JFK clips are used seamlessly to aid in this (Vaughn says he wants the sequel to open with the JFK assassination). What really sells this film is the amazing story that the events are all tied around. There are also some genuine good laughs and many in-jokes that don't detract from story at all.     The final set piece is where the film really reaches its best moments, despite any arguable missteps in getting there, it truly grips the audience member/X-fan and all the pieces come into play for what has to happen in the most terrific and the most tragic of ways (despite Mystique's growth being rushed). The final moments of that set piece are indeed the film truly living its full potential in rebooting this franchise.     Overall I give it 4.5 stars as a comic book movie and 4 stars as a film on its own. I want to leave room for the promise of a much improved sequel. It is undoubtedly one of the better comic book movies that will come out this summer (if not the best) and attempts admirable depth for a summer blockbuster, despite not quite finding that \\"place between rage and serenity\\" (as Charles tells Eric). Get out there and see it if you are a fan, it's worlds better than the cluster of plots that bogged down both X3 and X-men Origins: Wolverine. Lastly and most importantly, THIS FILM IS FUN!

I have to admit that until I reached the end of the novel I would have recommended this book to another person; yet, after reaching the twist at the end of the novel, that received little to no pages uncovering it further, I realized that through my knowledge of the novel itself and my feelings toward Picoult's other novel, the Pact, I should have expected the ending I received. To start, I was tricked by a plot that appears to be forever unraveling, but I warn any person who feels they may be interested in this book that the entire novel, approaching the ending, is exactly that, a trick. After reaching the twist at the end of the novel any reader can find themselves realizing that all Picoult did was come up with a story line that she felt compelled to add a \\"soap opera ending\\" to, which in turn obliterated the work as a whole. Upon reaching the twist I found myself shocked that the book ended in approximately 20 pages after. Picoult introduced this twist and then ended the novel with a nearly picture perfect ending *spoiler* of Alex being pregnant with Patricks baby, as if to say, \\"look at me! I managed to change the whole story around and end the book perfectly in approximately 20 pages!\\" I was completely infuriated that not only did she twist the entire plot and fall through on its elaboration, but she ended the novel in nearly the cheesiest way possible. I graduated high school last week and can say with 100% confidence that the way high school is depicted in this novel is completely taken over the top. Yes, high school has cliques, but they ARE NOT as Picoult depicts them. Cliques are present because people flock toward those who are like them, which is what people need in high school; therefore, they are not so much a cut throat food chain as she describes, but a part of human nature that exists even outside of high schools. Picoult makes high school appear far more dramatic than it actually is. While she does focus on the issue of bullying , which is something people need to be aware of - as I studied it partially in my senior project-, Picoult's portrayal of it is disturbingly uneducated. If she wanted to communicate a message, it would have been better sought through focusing less on stereotypes and on more realistic accounts. Lastly, I understand that DAs (prosecution) and defense attorneys are often portrayed as childish, but Pilcoult took it to an unprofessional, unrealistic level, where Jordan and Diana felt like two kids arguing. While this might have been an underlying dig at the legal system, it was on Picoult's part flat out rude to show these two individuals the way she did. Ultimately, I felt let down by this book more than I did The Pact, and I would not recommend it, but I would recommend to one who is interested in school shootings to read actual accounts of such events, as well as studies. However, if books that do not have sufficient endings that also take reality past reality interest you, go ahead and read this book.

After leaving their cutting edge genetics lab on a futuristic hover jet, the X-Men are forced to watch JFK give updates on a static black-and-white television.<br /><br />Still, it's awesome to have a real president overseeing these things for once. X-Men First Class isn't gory, but it does have some brutal murders. Another mutant can grab hold of average people and teleport them a mile into the sky.  Then he drops them.  This is a far cry from the horrors of Superman II, where the biggest danger was in having your bus tip over.<br /><br />There's a dark side even to the good guys, and many of the mutants are not above using their sexuality as a manipulation tactic.  Angel makes a living as an exotic dancer.  Emma Frost has no problem telepathically simulating a make-out session. Let's face it, when even Professor X is dropping the same genetic-theme pick-up line on every hottie at the bar, you've definitely crossed into new X-Men territory.<br /><br />If the movie falters anywhere, it's in bringing back that ridiculous blue gorilla suit.  Nicholas Hoult's character undergoes a transformation from a guy with big feet to The Beast, later (earlier) played by Kelsey Grammer.  While some comic book costumes look good on screen, this one is never gonna work.  He looks like a werewolf smurf, and might better off chasing Gargamel's cat through a magical candy forest.  A better solution would have been to show the beginnings of Beast's transformation, then to have him flee the movie out of shame, which would have been entirely within character.<br /><br />All told, X-Men First Class has catapulted itself to the upper echelon of comic book movies, into the heady space occupied by Dark Knight and Iron Man.  It does make one wonder if they will quit while they're ahead. B004RQVVGU|5.0|One need not be affiliated with the military to be familiar with a battle which took place in the early days of the Vietnam War. The battle of Ia Drang has been immortalized in retired General Hal G. Moore's best-selling book We Were Soldiers Once... and Young, which subsequently, Paramount made into a major motion picture. This particular battle is significant for various reasons. New concepts were tested against a new enemy, thus many \\"first\\" occurrences took place as the battle unfolded. This battle would be the first major engagement between the regular forces of the People's Army of North Vietnam or North Vietnamese Army (NVA) and U.S. ground forces. The venerable Bell UH-1D Iroquois (Huey) helicopter, the war horse of the Vietnam War, will be utilized for the first time in sustained combat operations for both troop transport and casualty evacuation. The concept of the Airmobile or Air Assault Infantryman will be put to the test for the first time against a formidable opponent. Essentially, this battle set the stage for future combat operations in the 10 year U.S. involvement in the Vietnam conflict.  The Ia Drang river valley sits just Nort East of the Chu Pong Mountain (also called Chu Pong Massif) or Hill 542 between two major rivers, the Ia Drang River to the North and the Ia Tae River to the South, both generally running from North East to South West. The Chu Pong Massif was a key strategic piece of terrain for both the North Vietnamese Army and U.S. forces. As stated in a Vietnamese military maxim: He who controls the Central Highlands, controls South Vietnam. The statement couldn't be more definitive and clear. The Central Highlands of Vietnam was long viewed as the central corridor of NVA movement, and was widely considered the most probable course of action the North Vietnamese would take if they were to launch a major offensive against South Vietnamese forces. It is important to understand the terrain in which this battle takes place and why seizing the Central Highlands was important for both sides.  The Central Highland region is sparsely inhabited. Traveling West, the terrain becomes more rugged, with mountains as high as 3000 ft bordering Cambodia. Triple canopy jungle makes up much of the vegetation at lower elevations, which makes for excellent covered and concealed routes. A main supply route used by the North Vietnamese, the infamous Ho Chi Minh Trail, was a primary area of interest for U.S. commanders and was frequently monitored. The area surrounding the landing zone in which the battle takes place is covered with a mix of tall elephant grass and stunted hardwood. A natural dry ravine runs North to South just West of the U.S. defensive position.  Prior to the battle, the North Vietnamese 33rd Regiment attacked a Special Forces base in Plei Me in October 1965, but were repulsed by the 12 man Special Forces team and the 350 Montagnard mercenaries garrisoned at the base, and a Battalion of Army of the Republic of Vietnam (ARVN) forces. This essentially set the stage for the 1st Cavalry Division to launch Operation Silver Bayonet, which was the first large-scale operation of the Division. The 1st Briagade conducted air assault missions throughout the area of operations in order to seek out and attack suspected enemy locations. The S-2 they received at the time was sketchy at best, and Operation Silver Bayonet initially didn't yield any tangible results. The 1st Brigade was eventually replaced by 3rd Brigade, and were given a mission to patrol the area surrounding Plei Me. Elements of the 3rd Brigade patrolled for three days, but never regained contact with enemy forces. The 1st Battalion, 7th Cavalry, 1st (Air) Cavalry Division led by LTC Harold G. \\"Hal\\" Moore, was then ordered to air assault into the Ia Drang Valley. Their mission was to find and kill the enemy.    U.S. Forces - 1st Battalion, 7th Cavalry RGT under the Command of LTC Harold G. Moore:  # personnel committed to the operation:  UNIT- OFFICER- ENLISTED  A CO- 5- 115  B CO- 5- 114  C CO- 6- 106  D CO- 4- 76    Total= 430    LTC Hal Moore's Air Cavalry troopers were thoroughly trained in the relatively new concept of being air lifted via UH-1D and inserted into landing zones to assault key objectives. This battle concept became known as an air assault, and was seen as the future of modern warfare. Though LTC Moore's battalion underwent extensive training prior to deploying to the combat theater of operations, the movement and loss of trained troops and key leaders proved to significantly reduce the combat strength of 1st Battalion, 7th Cavalry prior to conducting major military operations. Still, the morale of his troopers was high, which seemed to balance out the shortage of personnel committed to the mission. His men were equipped with standard M-16 assault rifles, M-79 40mm grenade launchers, M-60 machine guns, frag grenades and enough food and water to sustain them for a short fight. He would have 16 UH-1D choppers from A Co. 229th Assault Helicopter BN at his disposal to air lift his men, 2 batteries of 105mm artillery for indirect fire support from a firebase called LZ Falcon just West of Plei Me, and close air support from Air Force fighter wings. An aerial reconnaissance was conducted prior to the operation, but revealed little enemy activity. Prior to the assault, Landing Zone X-Ray was chosen as the primary landing zone. LZ X-Ray was located at the base of the foothills just NE of Chu Pong Massif. The LZ X-Ray and the foothills were to be prepped with artillery and aerial bombardment via rocket-equipped choppers to soften up any opposition in the AO. Elements of 2nd BN, 7th Cav was in reserve. The U.S. forces were prepared to bring to bear high-tech weaponry against a numerically superior force.    66th NVA Regiment, B-3 Front (PAVN/NVA) Division and H-15 Viet Cong under the Command of Deputy Commander Sr. LTC Nguyen Huu An:  UNIT Estimated# Of Troops  66th NVA Regiment 1600  H-15 Viet Cong 600Est. Total 2200 (to include elements of the 32nd NVA RGT)    The NVA Division, the B-3 Front, operating in the Central Highlands was under the command of Brigadier General Chu Huy Man. He was charged with tactical and administrative control over the PAVN and the Viet Cong, which were a communist guerilla force. The PAVN units were 320th, 33rd and 66th Regiments. The Deputy Commander, Senior Lieutenant Colonel Nguyen Huu An, was the Deputy Commander of B-3 Front conducting operations in and around the Chu Pong Massif. His forces had fortified bunkers and defensive fighting positions all along the slopes of Hill 542. The North Vietnamese objective was not to just simply control the Central Highlands, but to study the tactics, techniques and procedures of their new adversary. The NVA wanted to know how to fight U.S. forces by gauging the strengths and weaknesses of American forces. They wanted to see how the Americans employed its new technology, and come up with a strategy to defeat it. In other words, the North Vietnamese were just as anxious to pick a fight with the United States as the U.S. was ready to prove and battle test the lethality of its new airmobile concept. The NVA regulars and Viet Cong were equipped with Soviet made weaponry. AK-47 assault rifles was their weapon of choice, and RPGs, frag grenades was also the standard. As stated earlier, the numerically superior Vietnamese force was facing its high-tech opposition for the time. Morale among the NVA and Viet Cong troops was high. They had the advantage of having a better understanding of the terrain, having more personnel to conduct operations, and having control of the high ground. In addition to that, the NVA had an additional 2 Regiments, the 320th and the 33rd, operating in the immediate area to provide reinforcements. The B-3 Front's mission was simple: Lure the American forces into battle in order to learn how they fight.  The stage was set, and the two opposing forces were about to square off in the first major battle in the Vietnam War.    Prior to the first UH-1D touching down on LZ X-Ray, the battlefield was literally bombarded with artillery, accompanied by rocket-equipped helicopters. LTC Moore estimated that he could only load up to 3/4 of a Company onto the choppers per lift. Each lift would take approximately 30 minutes round trip to ferry troops to the battle. Although he managed to get at least 2 companies into position before the enemy reacted, it would still take over 4 hours to bring his entire Battalion into the fight. At approximately 1048 hrs, the first lift landed with elements of Bravo Company and the HQs element. There was no initial contact made with the NVA forces at this point. Bravo Company proceeded to move to secure the Western sector of the LZ. Upon conducting their initial sweep, they captured an enemy NVA soldier, who was in the area and was evidently caught off guard by the rapid ascension of U.S. soldiers onto the LZ. The NVA soldier had informed them that there were 3 battalions were on Chu Pong Massif who very much wanted to engage and destroy American forces, but were not able to find any. Bravo Company was then ordered to move to cover the Western flank of the LZ and to push the perimeter further out. This move was meant to allow time to keep the LZ open long enough in order to get the rest of the Battalion in place. At approximately 1120 hrs, the second lift arrives at the LZ with the remaining elements of Bravo Company and the first half of Alpha Company, who for the most part was charged with securing the South Western corner of the perimeter, which would prove effective when tying in with Bravo Company later during the course of the battle. At 1210 hrs, the third lift arrives with the rest of Alpha Company and LTC Moore was able to make a tentative push Westward to locate the enemy. At that time, Bravo Company had run into enemy contact which prompted the initial firefight of the battle. The dry creek bed or ravine that ran North to South along 1/7 Cav's Western flank proved to be an invaluable piece of terrain. It was considered to be a high-speed avenue of approach for the NVA forces to move straight off the mountain and onto the LZ. It was vital 1/7 Cav to retain control of that dry creek bed at all cost. A platoon from Bravo Company came into contact with what appeared to be a flanking element of the NVA. The NVA soldiers spotted the American troops, executed an about-face and began hauling ass out of the AO. Rather than closing ranks with the rest of Bravo Company, the Platoon Leader led his men on a dead run to catch the fleeing enemy, consequently separating his platoon from the rest of Company and Battalion. This resulted in a classic meeting engagement with the NVA forces. While pinned down, the NVA troops poured down the slopes and cut the platoon off. This, arguably, became the Achilles heel so to speak of 1/7 Cav's battle plan, as many men were lost from that platoon, and many more lost when sent to try and retrieve them. The \\"Lost Platoon\\" as they would be later referred as was isolated and surrounded by a superior number of enemy forces. Bravo Company is now heavily engaged in fighting along the Western flank against the oncoming NVA hoard making its way down the mountain, descending upon the numerically inferior American forces who realize that they must not allow their ranks to be broken until the rest of the Battalion arrives. Having bogged down Bravo Company, the NVA attempts to seize the opportunity to exploit their flanks, and NVA forces begin to maneuver a battalion sized element south of the LZ. At 1335 hrs, the fourth lift arrives with elements of Charlie Company, who quickly moves to secure the Southern portion of the LZ. Alpha Company then ties in with Bravo Company. At approximately 1400 hrs, there is a lull in the fighting as the two sides both wait for reinforcements to arrive. A single machine gun team from 3rd Platoon, Alpha Company was able to holdthe line and prevent the NVA from pushing through the defense. With each wave of American forces being airlifted in, more waves of NVA forces poured down of the Hill 542 to challenge them. The rest of Charlie and Delta Company were finally brought in. Delta Company proceeded to secure the Eastern flank of the LZ. Then, a RECCE (scout) heavy gun platoon was flown in to provide security to the TOC, secure the Northern side of the LZ, and take up defensive positions in the South Eastern corner of the LZ and covering Charlie Company's flank. Bravo Company, 2nd Battalion, 7th Cavalry was then flown in as reinforcements and secure the gap between Alpha and Charlie Company in the South West corner of the LZ. The other two platoons from Bravo Company took up defensive positions in the North. At this point, the U.S. forces have generally created a wagon wheel so to speak. 1/7 Cavalry sustained heavy losses and the 2nd Battalion reinforcements provided some relief. On the enemy side, their objective was to try and break through the lines, forcing the U.S. into a close quarter combat situation, which would render the U.S. indirect fire support ineffective. However, the 1/7 Cav's success in repelling the enemy assault proved costly to the NVA. Eventually the battle wore down before nightfall, with both sides sustaining a significant number of casualties. There were light skirmishes and enemy probing throughout the night, but for the most part the battle came to a standstill. The worst fighting was yet to come.  Throughout the night, the NVA sent out probes and various skirmishes took place in around the 1/7 Cav's defensive perimeter. The lost platoon, who had lost their Platoon Leader earlier in the fight, were battle weary but determined to fight to the end.  The following morning, the NVA resumed their attack and nearly punched a hole through Charlie Company's defensive position. The H-15 Viet Cong launched an aggressive and unforgiving attack on Charlie Company's Western Flank. A platoon from Alpha company and elements of the fragmented scout platoon were shifted over to plug the hole in Charlie Company's line. Had the Viet Cong been successful in their objective and were able to punch through, the LZ would've easily been taken, and the aftermath would have been grave for the men of 1/7 Cav. LTC Hal Moore called in a \\"Broken Arrow\\", a command indicating that an American Battalion was being heavily engaged and was in danger of being overrun. It was the code word used to bring to bear the full weight of every available element of U.S. firepower to bear on progressing enemy forces. Although this proved effective, it would also cost the lives of U.S. soldiers as well. Eventually, after taking a serious ass whuppin', Charlie Company was reinforced with elements of A/2/7 and B/2/7. In the end, Charlie Company, which started out with 106 officers and enlisted, would lose 42 men KIA and 20 WIA.  After 3 days of sustained combat, 1/7 Cavalry was relieved with its sister Battalions and combat operations continued in the AO. The lost platoon was eventually retrieved, and the wounded and dead were all accounted for and brought home. In the after action report, it was recorded that 634 PAVN/Viet Cong were killed, an estimated 1215 wounded, and 6 captured. U.S. casualties amounted to 70 KIA, 121 WIA and zero missing or captured.  Did the opposing forces meet their objectives? The objective of the B-3 Front was to lure the American forces into combat to see how they fought and employed their equipment. The PAVN met that goal, but at a tremendous loss. They nearly succeeded in punching through 1/7 Cav's defense. The PAVN proved to be a formidable enemy who clearly demonstrated that they're willing to make huge sacrifices for their cause.  From the U.S. perspective, 1/7 Cavalry was successful in accomplishing its mission, which was to find and kill the enemy. The 1/7 Cavalry not only found and killed the enemy on his terrain, but proved the effectiveness of air mobility and the use of superior fire power to achieve those goals. Although 1/7 Cav themselves sustained significant losses, they were successful in bloodying the nose and repelling a numerically superior force.

When I heard that the new X-Men film was going to be a prequel to the current X-Men movie franchise, I was a bit underwhelmed, but hopeful.  Having seen and loved Kick-Ass, which was also directed by Matthew Vaughn, I started to move toward cautiously optimistic. This film is.<br /><br />The heart of the film is the friendship between Charles and Erik, the young men who will eventually become Professor X and Magneto, the leaders of the two sides in the war between Humans and Mutants.  James McAvoy and Michael Fassbender both turn in amazing performances, especially Fassbender, who plays Erik.  When you are watching him on screen, you can see a tide of black emotions seething just under the surface. B000JQUQZO|5.0|The Roman Emperor Marcus Aurelius wrote his 'Thoughts' between 170 and 180. Other titles assigned to the same book are: 'Personal Notes', 'Meditations', 'The Meditations of Marcus Aurelius' et al. It is one of the few complete works of a late Stoic philosopher that still exists today. He wrote his 'Thoughts' as personal notes for himself. He writes about solidarity, physical adversity, good and evil, inner freedom and more. 'Thoughts of Marcus Aurelius' is a book full of wisdom that brings comfort and contemplation; it is moving and inspiring. I highly recommend it.<br /><br />This edition was originally translated into English by George Long in 1862 and edited by Edwin Ginn in 1893. Ginn has written the first 8% of the Kindle edition (preface, biographical sketch), and the last 15% (on the philosophy of Marcus Aurelius Antoninus). The 'Thoughs' of Marcus Aurelius are grouped in 12 'books' (chapters). The first book is clearly different from the other eleven; it is a 'thank you' to people who have had a good influence on him. For example: 'From my grandfather Verus (I learned) good morals and the government of my temper.' (I.1). The other eleven books contain his notes. His Stoic philosophy emphasizes ethics, especially everyday problems. This book is in the public domain and can be downloaded for free from several websites.<br /><br />Some quotations from this book:<br />Since it is possible that thou mayest depart from life this very moment, regulate every act and thought accordingly. (II.11)<br />Be cheerful also, and seek not external help nor the tranquillity which others give. A man then must stand erect, not be kept erect by others. (III.5)<br />Always run to the short way; and the short way is the natural: accordingly say and do everything in conformity with the soundest reason. For such a purpose frees a man from trouble, and warfare, and all artifice and ostentatious display. (IV.51)

B0049P1VHS|4.0|I'm not a big fan of the comic series this is based on; don't get me wrong, I read a lot of it and enjoyed a fair amount, but after a certain point all the tragedy started to feel more comical than dark the more it was piled on, and I had to quit. The narrative at times just felt like it was too big for its chosen medium, and the characters I cared about were vastly outnumbered by the characters who I couldn't care less for because they didn't get enough \\"page time\\" to really develop.    What I was most surprised by was how good the television series is at making characters the comic had painted as villains believable and sympathetic. While Comic-Shane was little more than a mentally unstable lumbering brute, TV-Shane comes across as a still unstable but very lonely man torn between his loyalty to his best friend and his own desires. Sarah Wayne Callies as Lori does an absolutely amazing job of turning a character I previously felt was little more than a shrill, selfish, hateful witch into a strong, conflicted woman I genuinely cared about and felt bad for. Andrew Lincoln does a good job as Rick Grimes, although he hasn't really had a chance to do much beyond look determined/horrified, and Steven Yeun is supremely enjoyable as fan-favourite Glenn. Carol's character gets a drastic overhaul as a badly abused wife (or at least her husband is present here where he was absent in the comic), but I feel it gives her some sorely needed perspective and character development that her often seemingly emotionally (and maybe mentally) unstable pen-and-ink incarnation lacked.    It does disappoint in some places. Too many of the new characters are utterly unforgettable to the point that deaths that are supposed to be tragic just come across as \\"meh\\", and while the violence is mature without being sadistically gory, I felt like the narrative let me down in a few places that it deviated from the source material. One character, for example, is significantly older than they are in the comic, and I have a feeling that it was a decision that was made solely to make the May-December romance that pops up less \\"weird\\" to the viewing audience, which was a bit of a disappointment when the comic managed to portray it in an honest, mature fashion.    But while the story does deviate drastically from the source material in a way that will probably enrage die-hard comic afficianados, the television incarnation of The Walking Dead manages to be that rare beast that balances action and horror with genuine, believable human drama without one ever really getting in the way of the other. The season finale is a bit over-the-top in that it strays a bit too far into formulaic sci-fi disaster movie territory, but at this point, I have put my trust in the cast and crew to deliver. Highly recommended.

B000QCS8TW|3.0|While Martin has a knack for creating interesting characters, the Game of Thrones and the rest of the series aren't exactly what you might call action-packed. The problem with such an enormous cast of characters is that you're bound to find characters you love over characters you find boring, and it can be a long, long time before the narrative cycles around to whoever you're more interested in hearing about. As you might expect from its title, the series really is one massive fantasy conspiracy/political thriller, and at times the pages and pages of conversations detailing who is double-crossing whom or who is trying to suss who out as a traitor can really make your eyes glaze over.<br /><br />An alternate title might also be The Game Where Nothing Nice Ever Happens to Anyone (And If It Does, Something Worse Happens Immediately Afterwards). To put it bluntly, for a lot of the cast the series almost comes across as psychological torture porn, particularly in the case of the young female leads who are consistently degraded and abused, but really nobody is safe from having multiple, emotionally scarring tragedies befall them in every book. It winds up getting tedious, and you can't help but wonder what the point of it all is. Who cares if this person is rescued? She's only going to get raped and murdered later. Who cares if this person wins a duel? They'll probably be forced to watch their kingdom burn next chapter.<br /><br />Ultimately, this series requires a lot of commitment, and it wasn't one I was willing to give. After reading the first four books I had to call it quits. It didn't feel like the characters were getting anywhere, and the plot was moving like molasses in winter. While there were characters I enjoyed (and even loved a little), the whole thing is too plodding and gloomy to really feel like anything more than a chore, and I didn't feel like seeing what terrible thing was going to happen to Sansa next. As of book four, it didn't feel like any real headway had been made in the plot, unless the plot was \\"the world is a terrible place, and no matter what you do, it will take a big dump on you at the moment you're happiest\\". Make no mistake, if you enjoy meticulously detailed worlds and can keep up with its labyrinthine treacheries and ever-growing cast, the Song of Ice and Fire series is definitely worth a look. B003Y3MYYU|5.0|Edit 12/24/13:<br /><br />Go to amazon.co.uk or amazon.de and buy the 2013 edition over the one this review is listed under.<br /><br />[[ASIN:B00BHNQ1N4 Richard Wagner Nibelungen Remastered Burmeister]]<br /><br />It's only 12 discs, with Walkre and Siegfried on 3 each with all the bad breaks removed. The Gtterdmmerung act III disc break is still present, though. Sound is a different remaster, but it sounds better IMO, but honestly not that different. A bit less background \\"fuzz\\" (also noticed this on the complete versus highlights of Karajan's Vienna Fledermaus), but both are still quite clear and excellent quality.<br /><br />Buying from the US is expensive as it is an import, and I paid $45 for it from Germany with expedited shipping. Germany and UK allow foreign currency and shipping too.<br /><br />Original Review 2011:<br /><br />This Ring Cycle is often listed on the top of critics' lists, and for good reason.<br /><br />First and foremost is Karl Bhm's superb conducting. Anyone who has heard his Mozart is in for a shock. He is so relentlessly fast that he makes Solti look like an old crone driving 30 mph on the freeway. But the force at which he conducts enhances the drama, as you are swept into a chaotic and brutal world of Gods, Dwarfs, Giants, Dragons, and (eventually) Humans. While the speed is not always well suited to certain scenes, he manages to craft his tempi in such a way that you cannot help but focus almost solely on the drama unfolding onstage. Perhaps this is one recording that would be better on video.<br /><br />The cast is fantastic as well. While some of members are past their respective primes vocally (Greindl, Mdl, and Neidlinger sound old, Windgassen as dry as cement, Rysanek a bit tired), everyone is dramatically effective and create wonderful performances. Nilsson manages to surpass her studio performance for Solti (one of, if not THE, best Brnnhildes on record) by her sheer involvement in the role if not always vocally.Perhaps the most amazing thing about this recording is that she still has the stamina to belt out the Immolation Scene after more than 4 hours on the final evening. Windgassen is still Siegfried even if he is huffing and puffing a bit at the end; King manages to outdo himself as Siegmund, and NOBODY has yet to equal his performance here; Adam has a powerful, if extremely dry voice, and is extremely involved as Wotan; Mdl is too tired to be an extremely effective Waltraute, but her involvement and dedication are outstanding; Stewart is not Uhde or Fischer-Dieskau, but his Gunther is enjoyable and better than some of the others out there; Wohlfarht is a nasty and bitter Mime, rivaling Stolze is vocal ugliness; Bhme is as frightful as ever; Nienstedt makes a brutish and positively EVIL Hunding, almost surpassing Frick and Greindl; Rysanek is a dedicated Sieglinde, whose chemistry with King is fantastic; Niedlinger and Greindl need no description. Smaller roles are taken well, with Anja Silja nearly stealing the show as Freia, and Dernesch, Wagner, and  make some of the best Rhinemaidens on record.<br /><br />The Bayreuth orchestra was never first class, and are probably at their worst here, (the trumpets in the Trauersmarsch sound like they are performing a Morricone score), but the way Bhm leads them, and the set back acoustics make the listener forget this the instant the vocals start.<br /><br />The sound is pretty good, with everything coming in clearly and well. For anyone who has heard Keilberth, while the orchestral sound was better there, here everything is clearer and there is no echo. There is a large amount of stage and audience noise, the latter of which can be so bad it makes me want to pull a Jon Vickers (\\"Stop your damned coughing!\\"). For the most part, however, it does not obstruct the noise that badly, and even the occasional bad mic placement is tolerable. As for the remastering, I still only have the Phillips release, but guessing from the factthat Decca chose not to fix the track listing (it can easily fit onto 12 discs with each Act of Siegfried being less than 80 minutes) they may simply polished the Philips tapes, if at all.<br /><br />Bhm's cycle has a lot to offer, and despite its setbacks, it manages to eclipse several other cycles out their, and truly is a benchmark performance.<br /><br />Update:<br /><br />Having received the new Decca edition, I tell can that it has likely NOT been restored. I figured this out since I used to have the Phillips release (I sold mine to pay for the new one with a significant net profit), and I am very disappointed in Decca for pulling and EMI (repackaging an old edition and claiming it's \\"new\\"), especially since the track listing SUCKS (see above). The packaging is very nice, better overall than the Phillips release. It does not contain the photos, which is a let down, but since they were astonishing low resolution on the Phillips release (I have heard that the old old edition with the librettos has better pictures though), I am not too worried about this. The booklet is glossy and contains an entire track by track synopsis of the entire cycle, has a nice (if all to brief) essay on the recording, and lists the complete cast on the back of the box. The box is made to look like  a metal box with postage stamps on it, and is much better looking than the rather dark and dank version from Phillips.<br /><br />Anyone who already has the Phillips release should stay with it (I decided not too only because I fervently disliked the look of the box), but it is certainly nice to have a significantly cheaper edition of this monumental recording out there for people who are new to the cycle.

0553386794|3.0|This is the only book I've read in the series, so bear that in mind as you read on.<br /><br />As far as \\"Game of Thrones,\\" there were some things I liked, some things I disliked.<br /><br />World Building: Martin's world is well-painted and believable - largely based off European medieval-ism (though historically inspired by the War of Roses). He obviously knows his history and has painted well the gritty reality of centuries past. There are gods in this world, but whether they exist or not is left ambiguous. It is a twist on much fantasy literature, where gods and goddesses galore intervene in the affairs of the world. There is magic, but is mostly alluded to - it's hinted that magic played a larger role in the past than it does in the present age.<br /><br />Most fantasy I've read follows a rags to riches story - unknown boy becomes great hero, saves the day - Frodo Baggins, Rand Al'Thor, Richard Cypher, etc, etc. Not here. It follows the workings of the nobles from the get-go, and hardly ever gives attention to the peasantry or lower classes. But it's interesting to read fantasy where we get a high-low view rather than the low-high view.<br /><br />In all, the world building is very unique, compared to other fantasy novels. Not to say it's completely devoid of cliches - \\"an evil storm brewing in the north behind some sort of wall\\" has been done a lot.<br /><br />Characters: What irked me about \\"Game of Thrones\\" were the characters. Not that they were bad, or unbelievable...I just found it hard to root for any of them, because very little of them stand for what is good (and if they do, they are punished for it...severely). I like how Martin is challenging the cliche of fantasy = good vs. evil, and instead going for \\"realistic,\\" yet, at the same time, I prefer characters that are good, believe in the power of good, and we will fight for THAT instead of their own selfish motives and ambitions. There are people like that in the real world, though they admittedly have their faults, so it's not exactly \\"unrealistic.\\"<br /><br />I know moral ambiguity is sort of the \\"point\\" of this series, but personally, I prefer a happy ending. I'm not saying \\"Game of Thrones\\" is bad because of this...it's just a preference. Perhaps Martin could have handled this better to convert people like me, but maybe I'm asking too much.<br /><br />Plot: Martin's book suffers from the get-go what Robert Jordan suffers from \\"Dragon Reborn\\" onward...too many points of view going on at once. Even in a huge book like Game of Thrones, you can't develop eight characters when each of them only gets a short time on the stage. There are no main characters in Game of Thrones, so instead of feeling personally connected with them, you are like a distant observer watching a tragedy unfold. Maybe this is a good thing, because the book would otherwise be more depressing than it already is. When good characters died and evil triumphed, I found myself not caring either way. I feel like this could have been solved had Martin cut out some of the points of view, leaving only Eddard, Tyrion, and Dany, and perhaps Arya, who I found to be the most interesting and personal. If he had focused on and developed these more, the book would have been better. I wonder whether Martin cut some lives short - not out of \\"realism,\\" but because too many threads were weaving a literary Gordian Knot.<br /><br />By the way, the strongest story arc is Dany's. It won a Hugo award for a reason. Though her ending was kind of WTF.<br /><br />I could have gone in greater detail. Get Game of Thrones if you're looking for something different - whatever you think of it, you can't deny it's a cliche buster of a fantasy novel.I know moral ambiguity is sort of the \\"point\\" of this series, but personally, I prefer a happy ending. I'm not saying \\"Game of Thrones\\" is bad because of this...it's just a preference. Perhaps Martin could have handled this better to convert people like me, but maybe I'm asking too much. It's not that it's bad, by no means; it's just not as moving to me as their other offerings.    Still Life proves a great transition for Opeth from the earliest albums to the later, showing the incredibly dense complexity of which they were capable, without completely reaching that Blackwater Park moment.  If you're already a fan of Opeth, then you will not be disappointed with this album, I promise; I know my review may seem harsh, but I'm a big fan of this album.  Believe me: four stars for an Opeth album equates to five stars by any other artist.    If you're not quite sold on Opeth yet, and you're wondering where to start, I would recommend Blackwater Park or Watershed, or Ghost Reveries/Deliverance if you're already into death metal.
